%%***>>>text element-link:[[Social networks with pro and cons.excalidraw#^Strength > facts]]<<<***%%Dangers of social ^eOGpFK3V

Easy marketing ^1MK46nvn

Smart cities ^H2YroRqb

Access
Reliability
Resilience ^oR2v3L2Y

Resources ^0vBxFIPr

Governments and citizen relationship has been grately influenced by
ICTs which made this exchange and collaboration cheaper and easier. 
There are critiques to this since it only affected who has access
to internet and not all people do.  ^hHoOH2Ya

It is definitely true that democracy itself has changed thanks to ICTs. In part it also 
changed for the worst since with globalization it shifted some of the power
and influence to global organizations external to states. States has taken
some measures to contains this organisations. ^Y8712W5l

With ICTs and democracy it also came the possibility of more
dialogue between citizens and power.
this fenomenon brought what we call digital democracy, citizens can stay
more informed than ever, it is also much easier to know who your
representatives are and contact them. Overall citizens can contribute more
than ever and this is apparent also in the new petition system, where 
signatures are gathered and on 10000 signs the parliament has to
consider the topic and on 100000 they have to schedule a
discussion about it ^jmwPOnXq

Government services became cheaper than ever and the government
is also trying to reduce the costs as much as possible since it is
paid by tax payers. The fires effort was with the digital by default
project where new projects must be faced thinking about digitalisation
first. This also brought the government to develop a service manual
for new developments. Another example is the digitalisation of passports,
with the new changes passports can be reniewed fully online, however the first
time you register the passport you still have to go there in person,
this is because it require your signature in ordrer to verify your identity.
The signature is a form of biometric data and it provide both aithentication
and non repudiation. You can also use digital signatures now that use
encryption but that is not a form of biometric data ^SIWpXoig

With new ICTs and methodologies for delivering government services,
governments have always more data regarding the citizens at their
disposal. Data has became more and more important (see the section
on health sector), and since data is gathered from the citizen
for the citizen there are strong arguments sustaining that it should
be held as public data. Usually the argument sustain the fact that 
since the government is sustained by the citizens that data is really
property of the citizen and therefore should be publicly available. 
From 2009 a new program called Smarter government, thanks to ICTs, 
opened the data.gov.uk as a government service where they gather 
and public all collected non-persona data  ^lbQR851f

With personal data there is also the
worry of big organizations using it to sell
it or to make money in general violating
privacy of the citicens ^iOyUID32
